I had a consultation with Dr. Shahan Yacoubian last year in late July. He diagnosed my problem and told me I needed a hip replacement. I told him I was not ready to have it done at that time. He replied to let him know when I could not take the pain any longer which he said would be about a year. A year later to the week I could not take the pain and scheduled an appointment. <review>This review is for the Ortho Urgent Care:

TL;DR: For me, the moral of the story is to listen to your gut. If you feel like you aren't being listened to or taken care of, always get a second opinion.

Under OSS's care I ended up in the ER with a massive pulmonary embolism. Details for a more dramatic effect: I had blood clots in all 4 quadrants of my lungs. The response from the ER doctor who treated me was "I've never seen a case so sever".

If the PA's and nurses had just paid a little more attention to me this might have been avoided.

I was referred to OSS from a local urgent care to treat a fracture on the lower part of my fibula (broken ankle). This was a clean break, meaning they didn't have to reposition the bone or do any surgery.

I saw them a total of 3 times: Initial visit to put on cast, 2 week follow up and then a 4 week follow up.

At the time of my 2 week follow up I was complaining about an abnormal amount of swelling and what felt like a constant charlie horse in my calf. I've never broken a lower limb before, so I had no idea this was not normal. The suggested cure for this was elevate (even though I already was). On top of that, the cast that was applied during this follow up was significantly tighter then the previous cast (think even more circulation issues).

On my 4 week follow up the only reason the PA mentioned going to the ER was because I was complaining of shortness of breath. I was so weak that I had to use a wheel chair to get from my car to the front office. I was able to walk from my car to the office both of the previous visits. In hindsight I should have gone to the ER immediately after that visit. I ended up going to the ER the next day.

Never once did they mention the word blot clots or DVT despite my complaints. I'm 32 and don't have a history of blood clots, but you never know and it's always better to be safe.

I had to cancel my 6 week follow up with them (because I was just getting released from the hospital). I told the nurse why and while she said "so sorry for what happened" no one has followed up with me to check on the status of my injury. I chose to follow up with the Ortho that treated me in the hospital instead.

I understand mistakes are made and I am just thankful to be alive and didn't have to take a ride in an ambulance. But this mistake is now costing me thousands of dollars in hospital bills. I guess I should be thankful there is no lasting physical damage to my body. We put so much trust in medical practitioners it always feels like a betrayal when mistakes are made, especially ones this big.</review><Pictures>None<//Pictures><Resp>None</Resp><gmap_id>0x80c2bfc495f8294f:0xe54d4fcf0f4052fb</gmap_id></record>

< text>
Service was just fine, they absolutely try to make you feel welcomed. My problem was with the ingredients and recipes for the "shrimp" enchilada dish I had. The rice was very bland, no matter how much salt you put on it after they bring it out to you it still lacks the appropriate flavor. They are cheap on the shrimp, and what I mean is that they used tiny pre-cooked-frozen shrimp that you could get at any store. WOW, very bland, lacking flavor, the consistency for what a shrimp enchilada should be was a wasted opportunity. How could you mess up such an easy dish? The only good thing on my plate was the beans and even that was served COLD so god knows how long that was out. I have a huge appetite and I usually finish any plate in front of me. I had most the plate unfinished and I didn't even want to take it home. I seriously feel robbed that I paid $18 for such horrible slop. That's why I'm giving this restaurant a 2 star rating because the food was horrible and so were the prices, but it's not the waitress fault that the cook is dealing with inferior ingredients.<//text>

<name>Tamara Kennedy</name>< review>
New owners deep cleaned this place. The donuts are fresh even warm. The COFFEE IS BETTER THAN MY OLD FRIEND STAR BUCKS...I never thought that could be possible...but these people are experts. The warm donuts and kick ass coffee made my eyes roll back in my head..so whats an extra workout this is welllll worth the extra workout..I have to mention this...they are so nice..they remember your favorites...they remember you here..the second time under new owners i entered and the pretty lady behind the counter said "good morning how are you so nice to see you back to get the coffee you like so much? Black no sugar no cream...and one warm glaze? We have three kinds warm but all donuts here are fresh made from 3 in the morning until 5 minutes ago..". The words ,I'LL TAKE A DOZEN ,flew out of my mouth without regret..i ate only my share...although i admit my compulsion was to take a bite from all 12 therby claiming ownership and obligation to consume. However, I resisted. Come to this place it is off the hook...so just like i remembered from when i was little. Fresh donuts, super clean, strong perfect cofee not pissy cheap coffee but great roasted fresh ground coffee, and the best customer service ever! Ya gotta go no joke,</review>

<review>Beautiful drive and nice way to spend an afternoon. There is a bunch of different marked view points with nice sites and you can just stop along the way. There is also beaches if you want to get out and relax a bit. Get to see some of the golf courses and plenty of the ocean. Costs $10.50 to get in with a car, but if you stop at one of the money restaurants you get that back. Suggest stopping at the Inn at Spanish Bay at the end and having a drink and some food by the firepits and if you get there at the right time you can see the piper come in playing the bag pipes to close the course for the day. Great way to spend an afternoon in Carmel!<//review>< pictures>

< Review>
7 Mile Drive hugs the rugged Californian coastline and a $10.50 toll gave us access to the route, multiple stopping points and restroom facilities. Along the pleasant and easy drive we got to see the churning Atlantic smashing into the various rock formations, sending up plumes of sea spray. Some of the rocks are home to seals, sea lions, pelicans, cormorants and gulls. We were entertained for a decent amount of time by a very noisy sea lion trying to clear a patch of rock for his exclusive use, only for it to be refilled by pelicans the instant his back was turned. Golfing fans were enthralled by Pebble Beach Links golf course (venue for the 2019 US Open), where you can have lunch in the clubhouse even if you can‚Äôt fit in 18 holes.</Review>

Definitely worth the $10 admission to see some amazing coastal scenery and portions of one of the most iconic golf courses in the country. There's plenty of places to pull off on the side of the road and take in the sights, and I definitely recommend taking your time and checking out many of these spots. < Rating>
5< /Rating>
<review>17-Mile Drive is a scenic road through Pebble Beach and Pacific Grove on the Monterey Peninsula in California, much of which hugs the Pacific coastline and passes famous golf courses, mansions and scenic attractions, including the Lone Cypress, Bird Rock and the 5,300-acre Del Monte Forest of Monterey Cypress trees.
The drive serves as the main road through the gated community of Pebble Beach. Inside this community, nonresidents have to pay a toll to use the road.
Like the community, the majority of 17-Mile Drive is owned and operated by the Pebble Beach Corporation. The 17-Mile Drive is a 17-mile (27 km)-long scenic loop having four primary entrances - the main highway entrance at California State Route 1, and entrances in Carmel and Pacific Grove.
The 17-Mile Drive guide map you get at the gate will give a brief description of each point of interest, or you can check the 17-Mile Drive Map online. Allow 3 hours or more for the whole drive, especially if you stop to eat or take a lot of photographs.<//review><Pics>[{'url': <Rate>5< /Rate><Text>It is truly a beautiful stretch of the Earth with multiple pull offs for either a drive, bike, or walk.  All manner of wildlife can be seen including deer, cranes, sea lions, sea birds, and even a whale depending on the season.  Watching the waves crash on the rocks and the beach was an amazing experience.  I highly recommend it. (Be warned that if you are going to bike the road, there are some points where there is no bike specific trail)</Text>< Pics>

<user>115076003494006671829<//user><name>Deepak Sethi< /name><Time>1527961098755</Time><Rating>5<//Rating><text>A must see if you're visiting Carmel,  Bigsur or Monterey.  There's a small fee of $10 to enter but that's fairly negligible for the amount of breath taking views that you get off the Pacific Ocean.

Plenty of places to stop and park to see the flora and fauna and get close to the ocean.  There's an area of white sand beach which is mesmerizing in itself.  The drive is fairly mountainous but doable for an average driver.
It does get pretty crowded over holiday weekends so be prepared to be stuck in traffic and taking rounds to find a parking spot.<//text>< Pics>

<text>A very scenic drive just to the south of San Francisco/San Jose. Although very touristy, this place does have it's own charm. Entrance to the 17-mile-drive costs $10.50 and is very worth it. They‚Äôll give you a map of all the attractions at the start and there‚Äôs usually parking at each one with signposts explaining the history. At US$10.75, one can visit a drive to 17-Mile Drive and experience a life time opportunity. Entire route is awesome and full of spots on the way. Most of the spots, reasonably good information with pictures are displayed. On every mile, one can fascinate to see new spots. All spots are unique and different than the last one. < UserId.>
111495219028271756808< /UserId.>
<Name>Jubin Edachery<//Name>< date>
1505693396248< /date>
<rate>4</rate>< Text>
This is a nice drive along the ocean offering some great views. Lots of nice ocean views, big homes and overall CA coastal beauty.

Suggestions:
* Weekends (esp Summer) can be crowded (goes without saying)

* To get the best part, start at the Pacific Grove gate entrance (instead of the main Hwy 1 entrance) and get off the Carmel exit.

* The Inn at Spanish bay is a nice place for lunch (it's right at the start if you follow this route). But if you are on a budget, pack some food from the town of Pacific Grove (just before you enter) and eat at the picnic tables. Overall the food along the 17-mile drive is great but very pricey.

* The beaches along the drive are nice, but Carmel beach is nicer. So if you want to get into the water (it's cold no matter where you go on this coast), just view the beaches on the drive and once you get to Carmel, go to the beach there. It's much nicer (less sea weed too).

* End the day with some shopping and dinner at Carmel-By-the-Sea. Its a cute little town.< /Text>

<review>(Translated by Google) If you are doing the path of the Big One, you cannot miss this stop. Pebble Beach. It is a closed neighborhood that is accessed by paying $ 10 per car. They give you a map where they show you the different viewpoints.

It is divided by different stops that the map indicates. Paradores towards the Pacific Ocean, which hits the coast hard. Rocky beach sectors. Every landscape is incredible. What's more, surely you saw the classic photo of the Cipress, it is a tree in the middle of the rocks at the tip of the peninsula. Postcard characteristic of the area.
Amazing landscapes, beautiful home.

In this complex you will also find the famous pebble beach golf course, the site of several international tournaments. Undoubtedly a very complex court due to the winds in the area. One of its holes is right between the road and the sea.

But the coastal scenery is impressive. Despite being a short tour, each one offers a different landscape.

Ideal to do it with children, friends or as a couple. Do not miss this beautiful place. It is very accessible and it will surprise you.

You will also find the architecture of the area, imposing houses in the middle of this green forest. The song of the birds in the whole area is striking.

An activity to do as a family is the construction of Torres. At one of the first stops you will find a beach full of rounded, cream-colored rocks. Build the tallest tower you can as a family! That is very careful with your feet. If any rock slips it can hurt a lot.
This beach has tables and chairs, ideal for a stop on the trip, a picnic on the shore of the turquoise ocean.

<review>(Translated by Google) It is driving the # 17-MileDrive üöôüåä
This is a great coastal route to drive #PebbleBeach and #PacificGrove along the Pacific coastline of Cali #Monterrey. As the name suggests, this is a place where you can enjoy 17 miles of roads with beautiful natural scenery. If you enter the Pacific Grove Gate on the north side, you can turn the sea to the right, and Navi pointed out HWY Gate 1 on the south. Enter Gate HWY 1 and turn clockwise to find the viewpoint next to the coast. Within 17 miles drive you'll find a total of seven golf clubs and a golf course with their beautiful Pacific views. Open is said to be held.

The ghost trees, which have been shaped by the sea for a long time, and the #TheLoneCypress tree, which has survived 250 years at the edge of the cliff, should not be missed. Don't miss the #BirdRockVistaPoint, where you can see the sea lions and countless birds, and the #PescaderoPoint which is truly fantastic.

üìå Since this is a private property, you will need to pay $ 10.25 toll cash per vehicle.However, if you pay more than $ 35 for food and beverages at #Pebble Beach Resort, the resort staff will pay the tolls at checkout, so make sure you have your receipts. However, the #PebbleBeachMarket with a simple piece of cake, pudding, donuts and drinks, a medium-sized market such as a supermarket, and a souvenir shop will not be refunded if the purchase amount exceeds $ 35.

<Name>K. Franz W.</Name><text>(Translated by Google) A must if ...
... one on the most legendary car routes in the world,
the classic of California Highway 1 is on the way.

We had stayed in Carmel-By-The-Sea on our round trip through California.
Since the famous 17-Mile Drive was only a few kilometers away from our hotel,
we decided to take a look at this panoramic road that we had read and heard about so much.

Also for the sole reason that the "Lone Cypress" (Monterey cypress), which is famous in many photos and is over 250 years old, has become an institution over the years.
can be seen live at "Stop Number 16".

According to literature, it is probably the most photographed tree in the world.

Unimaginable that this wind-blown cypress on the small barren rock ledge directly on the coast
has survived for so long. The "Monterey cypresses" are part of a whole cypress forest, whose special species can only be found in this area

But also the "Ghost Tree" at "Stop number 17",
a dead Monetrey Cypress attracts the attention of many tourists.

It is written that a trip to California is only complete
if you've also taken a ride on the famous 17-Mile Drive.

We liked it and we can unreservedly recommend this beautiful stretch of coast with fantastic views of the sea, beach, rocks, trees, etc.

And so we hereby confirm the following self-promotion:

"One of the most famous scenic drives in the world"
Scenic Road leads you through Pacific Grove and Pebble Beach - a gated community.
